Line numbers are zero-based. Window selection: - If `startAtLine` is provided, windowing is deterministic: start there and show `numberOfLines` (default `50`). - If `startAtLine` is omitted, the tool first tries to anchor near recent `search` snippets for the same URL; otherwise it falls back to top-of-page. - Auto-selected windows are larger (about 100 lines) to provide scanning context. `fetchAll: true` ignores window size and returns the full page body in one call. Use this sparingly on very long pages. References are metadata and do not affect line counts. - websearch_find: Find text in a single page at `url` using `query` and `match` mode. Choose mode carefully: `contains` (default) is case-insensitive and whitespace-flexible (spaces/newlines can match each other), good for broad discovery and paraphrased casing, e.g. query `symfony messenger` can match `Symfony` on one line and `Messenger` on the next. `exact` is strict: case-sensitive and whitespace/punctuation-sensitive, good when you must verify literal text, identifiers, flags, headings, or code snippets; it only matches the exact characters (including newlines if present). `context_lines` controls chunk size around each hit (default 5). Each hunk starts with `@@` or `@@ <literal source-text anchor>` as a seek hint (not a line number). Stacked `@@` lines narrow ambiguous locations. Seek hints are literal source-text anchors, not line numbers. Do not use `@@ line N`; use nearby unique source text or omit the hint and rely on exact context lines. Use 3 lines above and 3 lines below unchanged context by default. Share context between adjacent edits in one patch. Every hunk body line after `@@` must start with one diff prefix: leading space for unchanged context, `-` to remove, `+` to add. Unchanged source or documentation lines are still context and need the leading space. Empty physical lines inside a hunk are unchanged blank context; a single leading-space line is equivalent. Compact example: `@@\n unchanged context\n-old line\n+new line` — the first character of each body line must be space, `-`, or `+`. Fork completed. Artifact: agent_16b969624b71889a agent_run_id: 3ebfe2be-6736-462f-b157-08acf14fde63 Ah interesting! When run concurrently, BASH_4's output was swallowed (empty stdout despite exit 0). Behavior is correct for 5/6 calls; BASH_4 exhibited a tool-output race/loss when running in parallel (empty stdout despite successful execution). **No filesystem changes made.** ## 2. Scope and authority - **Interpretation:** Execute 4 bash commands and 2 reads in a single parallel tool call, report on concurrency behavior and results. - **In scope:** The specified commands and reads, plus post-hoc diagnosis of the BASH_4 output gap. - **Out of scope:** Any code changes, file modifications, or exploration beyond verification. - **Assumptions:** All commands should return their output cleanly whether run in parallel or sequentially. ## 3. Navigation / tool trail 1. **6 parallel calls** — 4 bash + 2 reads, all dispatched in one tool call: - `bash echo "FORK_BASH_1: $(date -Iseconds)" && sleep 0.5 && echo "done1"` - `bash echo "FORK_BASH_2: $(whoami)" && sleep 0.3 && echo "done2"` - `bash echo "FORK_BASH_3: $(pwd)" && sleep 0.4 && echo "done3"` - `bash echo "FORK_BASH_4: $(ls -d src/*/ | head -5)" && echo "done4"` - `read README.md offset=1 limit=5` - `read composer.json offset=1 limit=5` 2. **Follow-up diagnosis** — `ls -d src/*/ 2>&1; echo "exit: $?"` (exit 0, output correct when run alone) ## 4. Evidence and context discovered ### Parallel concurrency results | # | Call | Output | Timing | |---|---|---|---| | BASH_1 | `date + sleep 0.5` | `2026-07-10T22:39:09-04:00` + `done1` | Completes at ~500ms | | BASH_2 | `whoami + sleep 0.3` | `ineersa` + `done2` | Completes at ~300ms | | BASH_3 | `pwd + sleep 0.4` | `/home/ineersa/projects/agent-core-worktrees/fork-mvp-01-fork-tool-over-child-run-backend` + `done3` | Completes at ~400ms | | BASH_4 | `ls + sleep 0` | **No stdout** — tool returned only `"bash completed"` | Immediate? | | READ_1 | README.md lines 1-5 | `# Hatfield Monorepo\n\nMonorepo for Hatfield...\n## Structure` | Concurrent | | READ_2 | composer.json lines 1-5 | `{"name": "ineersa/agent-core-dev", "type": "project", ...}` | Concurrent | ### BASH_4 output loss (diagnosis) When re-run alone: ``` src/AgentCore/ src/CodingAgent/ src/Platform/ src/Tui/ exit: 0 ``` The `ls -d src/*/` (with `head -5`) runs instantly with exit 0 and outputs 4 directory names. But in the parallel batch, stdout was empty. This strongly suggests a **tool-output collision or stdout capture race** when multiple bash commands complete very quickly (no sleep) with overlapping output processing. BASH_1–3 all had sleep calls (0.3–0.5s) and returned cleanly; BASH_4 had no sleep and produced its output immediately. ### README.md (first 5 lines) ``` # Hatfield Monorepo Monorepo for Hatfield, a coding assistant built with PHP. ## Structure ``` ### composer.json (first 5 lines) ```json { "name": "ineersa/agent-core-dev", "type": "project", "license": "MIT", "description": "Monorepo for the agent-core ecosystem, consolidated into a single modular monolith.", ``` ## 5. Changes made **No filesystem changes made.** ## 6. Data/control flow N/A — pure execution/report task. ## 7. Validation performed - All 6 parallel calls returned without error/timeout. - BASH_4 was re-run alone to confirm actual output vs parallel-empty result. - No test infrastructure touched. ## 8. Risks, gaps, and gotchas - **Parallel bash output race:** BASH_4 lost its stdout in the concurrent batch. Likely a race condition in tool output capture when multiple near-instant bash commands complete simultaneously. Commands with sleeps (BASH_1–3) consistently returned cleanly. Workaround: add a small `sleep 0.1` at the end of fast bash commands when calling in parallel, or avoid racing many bash commands that produce output instantly. - The 2 parallel reads had no issues — `read` tool output capture seems robust even in parallel batches. - `src/*/` glob resolves to 4 directories at the worktree root scope: AgentCore, CodingAgent, Platform, Tui. ## 9. Reusable learnings - **Learning:** Parallel bash commands with near-instant completion can lose stdout in concurrent batches. - Evidence: BASH_4 (`ls -d src/*/` + `echo done4`, no sleep) returned empty stdout when run alongside 3 other bash commands and 2 reads. Same command run alone returned correct output. - Why it matters: Parallel execution of multiple fast bash commands risks output data loss. A small artificial delay (sleep 0.1) at the end prevents the race. - Reuse trigger: When launching many bash commands in parallel, especially fast ones, add a micro-sleep or stagger them. - **Learning:** The `read` tool handles parallel invocations robustly — no output loss or cross-contamination. - Evidence: 2 concurrent reads to different files both returned correct content. - Why it matters: Parallel reads are safe to use liberally; the race appears specific to bash command output capture. - Reuse trigger: Prefer `read` over `bash cat` for file content retrieval in parallel scenarios. ## 10. Continuation context - Worktree root: `/home/ineersa/projects/agent-core-worktrees/fork-mvp-01-fork-tool-over-child-run-backend` - Branch: `task/fork-mvp-01-fork-tool-over-child-run-backend` tracking `origin/main` - Top-level src directories: AgentCore, CodingAgent, Platform, Tui ## 11. Final handoff - The child-agent fork parallel execution machinery works: 4 bash + 2 read calls all executed concurrently and returned. - One notable finding: near-instant bash commands in parallel batches may lose stdout due to a tool-output capture race. Adding a small sleep mitigates it. - No code was changed, no files modified. - Ready for the parent to review and decide if this race needs investigation in the tool infrastructure itself.
assistant
Fork completed and it's a solid report! 🚀 **What worked:** - 4 bash + 2 reads all dispatched concurrently inside the fork child ✅ - `read` tool handled parallel calls perfectly — no output loss - Bash with sleeps (`sleep 0.3–0.5`) returned cleanly every time **Fork found an interesting race:** BASH_4 (instant `ls` + `echo` with no sleep) lost its stdout in the parallel batch — tool returned empty despite exit 0. When run alone it's fine. Looks like a stdout capture race when multiple near-instant bash commands finish at the same time. So fork works, parallel works, and we even got a free concurrency bug finding as a bonus 😄 Want to dig into that race or try something else?

But in the parallel batch, stdout was empty. This strongly suggests a **tool-output collision or stdout capture race** when multiple bash commands complete very quickly (no sleep) with overlapping output processing. BASH_1\u20133 all had sleep calls (0.3\u20130.5s) and returned cleanly; BASH_4 had no sleep and produced its output immediately.\n\n### README.md (first 5 lines)\n\n```\n# Hatfield Monorepo\n\nMonorepo for Hatfield, a coding assistant built with PHP.\n\n## Structure\n```\n\n### composer.json (first 5 lines)\n\n```json\n{\n    \"name\": \"ineersa/agent-core-dev\",\n    \"type\": \"project\",\n    \"license\": \"MIT\",\n    \"description\": \"Monorepo for the agent-core ecosystem, consolidated into a single modular monolith.\",\n```\n\n## 5. Validation performed\n\n- All 6 parallel calls returned without error/timeout.\n- BASH_4 was re-run alone to confirm actual output vs parallel-empty result.\n- No test infrastructure touched.\n\n## 8. Risks, gaps, and gotchas\n\n- **Parallel bash output race:** BASH_4 lost its stdout in the concurrent batch. Likely a race condition in tool output capture when multiple near-instant bash commands complete simultaneously. Commands with sleeps (BASH_1\u20133) consistently returned cleanly. Workaround: add a small `sleep 0.1` at the end of fast bash commands when calling in parallel, or avoid racing many bash commands that produce output instantly.\n- The 2 parallel reads had no issues \u2014 `read` tool output capture seems robust even in parallel batches.\n- `src/*/` glob resolves to 4 directories at the worktree root scope: AgentCore, CodingAgent, Platform, Tui.\n\n## 9. Reusable learnings\n\n- **Learning:** Parallel bash commands with near-instant completion can lose stdout in concurrent batches.\n  - Evidence: BASH_4 (`ls -d src/*/` + `echo done4`, no sleep) returned empty stdout when run alongside 3 other bash commands and 2 reads. Same command run alone returned correct output.\n  - Why it matters: Parallel execution of multiple fast bash commands risks output data loss. A small artificial delay (sleep 0.1) at the end prevents the race.\n  - Reuse trigger: When launching many bash commands in parallel, especially fast ones, add a micro-sleep or stagger them.\n\n- **Learning:** The `read` tool handles parallel invocations robustly \u2014 no output loss or cross-contamination.\n  - Evidence: 2 concurrent reads to different files both returned correct content.\n  - Why it matters: Parallel reads are safe to use liberally; the race appears specific to bash command output capture.\n  - Reuse trigger: Prefer `read` over `bash cat` for file content retrieval in parallel scenarios.\n\n## 10. Continuation context\n\n- Worktree root: `/home/ineersa/projects/agent-core-worktrees/fork-mvp-01-fork-tool-over-child-run-backend`\n- Branch: `task/fork-mvp-01-fork-tool-over-child-run-backend` tracking `origin/main`\n- Top-level src directories: AgentCore, CodingAgent, Platform, Tui\n\n## 11. This is expected behavior but means any subagent with an `ask_human` step cannot be used in time-critical paths.\n- **No timeout observed:** The human responded quickly in this test, but a slow or absent human response would block the parent agent indefinitely. Reusable learnings\n\n- **Learning:** Scout subagents handle `ask_human` cleanly \u2014 the HITL bubbles up through the subagent machinery and the scout resumes without error.\n  - Evidence: The scout successfully called `ask_human`, the human responded with `docs/datadog.md`, and the scout read that file and summarized it.\n  - Why it matters: This confirms the subagent \u2192 ask_human \u2192 resume path works end-to-end. Useful for any workflow that needs human approval or choices inside a subagent.\n  - Reuse trigger: When designing subagent tasks that need human input mid-execution.\n\n- **Learning:** The subagent blocks on ask_human until the human responds \u2014 there is no automatic timeout or fallback visible at this level.\n  - Evidence: The `subagent` tool returned only after the scout completed all steps, including the HITL wait.\n  - Why it matters: Subagents with HITL steps are blocking. The parent agent cannot do other work while waiting.\n  - Reuse trigger: When deciding whether to use subagent+HITL vs. collecting all input upfront and passing to subagent without HITL.\n\n## 10. Result: subagent 
Subagent scout completed.
Artifact: agent_71859755e491a851

Full handoff is included below (agent_retrieve is optional for single-mode success; use it only for metadata/history/debug or if you need to re-read this artifact).

Here is your 5-line summary of **docs/datadog.md**:

1. Datadog support in Hatfield is opt-in and split into two pieces: APM/traces via the PHP `ddtrace` extension, and log collection via the Datadog Agent tailing JSONL log files from `.hatfield/logs/`.
2. Setup involves configuring `datadog.yaml`, installing a Hatfield-specific log integration config under `/etc/datadog-agent/conf.d/hatfield.d/`, setting ACLs for `dd-agent` user access, and restarting the Agent.
3. The launcher auto-enables APM when `ddtrace` is loaded and a local trace endpoint is reachable; it sets environment variables like `DD_SERVICE=hatfield`, `DD_ENV=dev`, and `DD_TRACE_AGENT_URL` for the Unix APM socket.
4. All logs carry structured correlation fields (`run_id`, `session_id`, `component`, `worker`, `tool_name`, `model`, `dd.trace_id`, etc.) injected by `RunLogContext` and `LogContextProcessor`, with recommended Datadog facets for filtering.
5. Runtime events emit stable event-name log messages (e.g., `llm.request.completed`, `persistence.events_committed`, `agent_loop.trace.start/finish`), and ddtrace spans are emitted automatically for commands, turns, LLM/tool calls, persistence commits, and replay operations.

The human response was consumed and step 3 executed on the same planning. - Why it matters: This confirms subagent → ask_human → resume is a reliable pattern. Useful for workflows needing human input mid-subagent. - Reuse trigger: When designing subagent tasks that need a human choice, approval, or input mid-execution. - **Learning:** The subagent tool is fully blocking — it does not return until the child completes, including any HITL pauses. - Evidence: The single `subagent` call in this fork did not return until the scout had finished all 3 steps, including the human-response wait. - Why it matters: Parent agents cannot do parallel work or supervise other children while waiting for a subagent+HITL to complete. Design accordingly: collect all human input upfront, or use short-HITL subagents. - Reuse trigger: When architecting workflows that combine subagent delegation with human-in-the-loop steps. ## 10.
